In Bjørvika at the raised intersection known popularly as the Traffic Machine, a carrier bag floated on the warm air currents above the roads, which wound in and out of one another like entangled vipers in a nest…</i><br/><br/>In the fifth Harry Hole thriller, the Oslo detec</span>
  <span id="freeText5033000728359998411" style="display:none"><i>Harry continued talking, interrupted by the excited voices of the others, as the sun arced high across the pale, scorched summer sky above the small white sails of boats making drowsy, half-hearted attempts to find their way back to land. In Bjørvika at the raised intersection known popularly as the Traffic Machine, a carrier bag floated on the warm air currents above the roads, which wound in and out of one another like entangled vipers in a nest…</i><br /><br />In the fifth Harry Hole thriller, the Oslo detective is drunk and distraught, living apart from Rakel and her 10 ten year old son, Oleg, his sleep wracked by nightmares and rarely turns up for work, protected by former hacker now taxi driver Øystein Eikeland and his superior, Bjarne Møller. We quickly learn that he has been forced to the edge of reason at his inability to corner the slippery and ambitious DI Tom Waaler, who Harry suspects is involved in arms smuggling, intimidation of witnesses and causing actual death to cover up his activities.<br /><br />The killing of a young woman who had her finger amputated ante-mortem and the disappearance of another brings Harry into the fold to reluctantly work with Waaler to secure a conviction, stemming from Harry’s successful unmasking of a serial killer in Sydney (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13532287.The_Bat__Harry_Hole___1_" title="The Bat (Harry Hole, #1) by Jo Nesbø" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bat</a>). When a third victim is found, the killings and disappearance are linked through blood diamonds, smuggled from Sierra Leone into Eastern Europe and shaped into a 5-point star, with a pentagram etched or left at the scene.<br /><br />At first this was a slow burner, lightened by the timely appearance and wit of psychologist Ståle Aune, who explains the difference in profiles of a psychopath (loner/misfit) and a sociopath (well-established, successful), for the benefit of the police and the reader. Throw in a Russian orthodox priest who explains ancient religious symbolism and forensic expert Beate Lønn and her assistant Bjørn Holm and a pattern begins to emerge, followed close by a suspect. But it’s Tom Waaler’s insistence at running the show that is his own undoing.<br /><br />Jo Nesbø’s plots are far from linear, but this one takes Harry full circle from nightmares to a living nightmare and his aversion to elevators. Minor characters make a cameo appearance that might be pure coincidence or misdirection. In a surreal sequence Harry questions a reluctant and unreliable witness on a detail on the person he saw, the man then walks his dog, allowing it to soil the footpath (witnessed by a woman in a house), crosses the road and passes a young woman running in the opposite direction. She unwitting steps in the turd and hails a taxi, both she and the driver exchanging glances at the pong, before she alights to meet her killer. Unsavoury and insanitary practices, Oslo wilting under a heatwave all play a part here, down to the finer details of breakfast and the digestive process.<br /><br />This was my fourth Harry Hole thriller, and far from being deterred, (de-turd?) I look forward to reading more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5033000728359998411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2901139372" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2901139372" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11251688-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590252155p2/11251688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2901139372?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/11251688-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061133985" href="/book/show/8429276-the-devil-s-star">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2901139372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7311653968616452250">Detective Harry Hole is cajoled into accepting a case working with a hated partner. The investigation points to a serial killer with specific methods, but seemingly no motive. Hole's personal life and demons always complicate matters. Set during a very hot Oslo summer, this suspenseful thriller doesn't disappoint. The author writes the best Nordic Crime Novels in my humble opinion.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3523681313" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3523681313" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3523681313?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=nordic-noir">nordic-noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=mystery-detective-thriller">mystery-detective-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3523681313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5489410546478488180">The Devil's Star is probably the best written of the Jo Nesbo's mystery thriller series starring Harry Hole I've read so far. As I have said, for no particular reason I seem to be alternating these Nesbo mysteries with the widly contrasting Agatha Christie series featuring the elderly (Miss) Jane Marple. The contrast, as you might imagine, is jarring, and calls forth the most obvious kinds of commentary about the literary and cultural differences in the fifty years between the time that the Marp</span>
  <span id="freeText5489410546478488180" style="display:none">The Devil's Star is probably the best written of the Jo Nesbo's mystery thriller series starring Harry Hole I've read so far. As I have said, for no particular reason I seem to be alternating these Nesbo mysteries with the widly contrasting Agatha Christie series featuring the elderly (Miss) Jane Marple. The contrast, as you might imagine, is jarring, and calls forth the most obvious kinds of commentary about the literary and cultural differences in the fifty years between the time that the Marples I am reading were written and the twenty-first century Holes. <br /><br />And the differences seem to be more and more marked. The Devil's Star is about three or four principal things: 1) Harry's dogged pursuit of a particularly brutal (as opposed to what, kind?) serial killer who leaves as one calling card (and clue) a jewel on each of his victims in the shape of a pentagram or "devil's star" associated withe demonology and the occult; 2) Hole's continuing obsession with his colleague Tom Waaler's (possible) role in the death of their mutual colleague Ellen; 3) Harry's alcoholism and despair, and 4) his relationship to Rakel, her son and the possibilities for a "normal life" with her.<br /><br />Harry is assigned to work on the serial killer case with his nemesis Waaler. They have a kind of Batman-Joker origin comparison going on here for me. Both have had traumatic losses that shape their rogue decision-making, their "outsider" or maverick status, their willingness to break the law to get results. Waaler wants Hole to join him in an enterprise that is illegal, but could create quicker and more dramatic results for Harry's purposes. Why not? What difference is there between Waaler and Hole? But there is a difference, and you know there is without even reading it.<br /><br />This is by far the darkest of the novels so far; Harry's despair/struggle with alconolism coincides with his never-ending obsession to solve his friend Ellen's case, and in the process damages his relationship with Rakel. And then there's all the serial killing itself, which seems to be a kind of set-piece for mystery/thriller writing (though if a kind of serial killer exists in Christie mysteries, they are never grisly, of course). At its worst in Nesbo, it can veer into "torture porn," (by which I mean it is supposed to get readers obsessed with the physical aspects of the killings; I don't literally mean pornography with torture in it) something I am not interested in at all, I am sick of mysteries about serial kilers, but at the same time, I was interested in how the pentagram in this story reminded me of Alan Moore's From Hell, which poses a pentagram/occult theory about the Jack the Ripper (also five) killings. <br /><br />And, I'll admit that I was interested in how the two main crime stories--about Waaler, and about the serial killer--come together in interesting ways, and the writing is sharper, more focused and faster than in any of the previous books. It's not often what you'd call pleasant, in fact almost never that, but Nesbo keeps getting better at his craft. And I like how in the end we don't yet know some important things: How deep is the corruption in the police department? Will Harry give up police work and say, drive a cab instead? Will his relationship with Rakel last? Set-ups for the next book, I think.<br /><br />The cover of my copy of the audiobook version I listened to announces (in a book published several years ago) that Nesbo has sold more than 25 million copies of his books in many languages, so it must be double that by now. Not quite what Christie has sold, but he's also got a few years and a few books to catch up to her. It's funny, both are great writers at what they do but I am somewhat unsatisfied with them for opposite reasons: One, this "cozy" mystery writer is usually too cozy and charming and light for me in these Marple books, but Nesbo has the opposite problem for me at times: He's just too brutal and nasty at the most extreme moments. As in, for those who have read it, the conversations between Harry and the serial killer that detail some of what he did, ugh. But maybe that's just me. <br /><br />One continuing nitpick: Why can almost no one pronounce Harry Hole's name correctly in these audiobooks!!?? (It should be like "Hoo-leh" and not Hole). In this one the reader pronounces it three different ways. But he never makes that mistake with the German in the text. Do your homework, dudes!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5489410546478488180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Steve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2330809-steve"><img alt="Steve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297342999p2/2330809.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/648228563?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve" href="/user/show/2330809-steve">Steve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061133985" href="/book/show/8429276-the-devil-s-star">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer648228563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18228262219370938839">Ouch, that was brutal (but that's the point, right)? First, if you don't know Harry Hole, do NOT start with this one. (Whether you try to read them in the order they were released in the US or in Europe - which, alas, is completely different - that's another story - but don't start with this one, which, arguably, is # 3 (US) or # 5 (Europe), but I can't confirm any of that). In any event, the whole cast (colleagues, friends, lovers, and those who are good, evil, and everything in between) is bac</span>
  <span id="freeText18228262219370938839" style="display:none">Ouch, that was brutal (but that's the point, right)? First, if you don't know Harry Hole, do NOT start with this one. (Whether you try to read them in the order they were released in the US or in Europe - which, alas, is completely different - that's another story - but don't start with this one, which, arguably, is # 3 (US) or # 5 (Europe), but I can't confirm any of that). In any event, the whole cast (colleagues, friends, lovers, and those who are good, evil, and everything in between) is back and remains in character. It's no spoiler to say that - compared to some others in the series, there's at least one huge surprise as to who dies and, to my mind, a surprising number of potential victims who are saved. Nesbo is in full stride for pretty much the entirety of this book, Harry is back in Oslo, and, as a result, the pages fly by, the body count rises, the carnage and tension escalate, potential distraction and feints are frequently introduced, and the whole comes together. Perfect plane and bus and hotel room reading, which is just what I needed. I'll be back for more.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5532761208529090665">Yahoo! Another of the dynamite, curious, loner Harry Hole book finished.   <span id="freeText5532761208529090665" style="display:none">Yahoo! Another of the dynamite, curious, loner Harry Hole book finished. My friend Harry R. said I have to read him, Jo Nesbo and his character, Harry Hole. <br /><br />I did not think, seriously, didn't think I would like Harry Hole. Put me in the Caribbean, the South Seas, Hawaii, anywhere there is beach and palm trees and I'm happy. But cold, dreary weather, not so happy. Hole is in Oslo, Norway! Where it's a heat wave at 77 degrees F.<br /><br />But after reading Harry R.'s first review, I thought...ok, Harry, my friend, I'll give your friend Harry Hole a spin. I am so glad I did. What a series. <b>WHAT a series!</b><br /><br />Enough said from me. Our Harry wrote the best review ever written (in my estimation) about Nordic writers and this one in particular, Jo Nesbo, and his excellent creation Harry Hole. With that said, please read Harry's review. It's an education on the Scandinavian writers who are so popular now. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/546324612?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry's Review of Harry</a> starring in <i>The Devil's Star.</i></span>

<div id="review_340454967" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/340454967" />
    <a title="Sasha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9925031-sasha"><img alt="Sasha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338538823p2/9925031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/340454967?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sasha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sasha" href="/user/show/9925031-sasha">Sasha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer340454967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16414367686480685593">Norwegian author Jo Nesbø made a big splash now after Stieg Larsson successful "Millenium trilogy" became publishing phenomenon - since Larsson is sadly deceased,attention focused on another writer from the north of Europe and Nesbø is advertised as "new Stieg Larsson". Well,not exactly.<br/><br/>Apparently Nesbø already wrote a whole series of successful crimi novels so this is just one of them,however this was my first introduction to his writing and I must say that I find them incredibly slow and suffe</span>
  <span id="freeText16414367686480685593" style="display:none">Norwegian author Jo Nesbø made a big splash now after Stieg Larsson successful "Millenium trilogy" became publishing phenomenon - since Larsson is sadly deceased,attention focused on another writer from the north of Europe and Nesbø is advertised as "new Stieg Larsson". Well,not exactly.<br /><br />Apparently Nesbø already wrote a whole series of successful crimi novels so this is just one of them,however this was my first introduction to his writing and I must say that I find them incredibly slow and suffered trough the whole book,expecting but not finding any of interesting quirks of Stieg Larsson (who could also be slow at the start but later gets towards completely original and unexpected turns). Honestly I don't get where all the fuss about Jo Nesbø comes from since the story is very usual serial killer plot with police going in circles and main character is alcoholic constantly suffering from hangover - like we never ever before encountered self-destructive policeman who don't know should he quit his job,divorce his wife or simply shut up and die. I persisted to the end,constantly expecting that something interesting will happen but it didn't and guess what,the killer was exactly the one I suspected from the start.<br />My impression is that publishing world simply needs new Stieg Larsson so now they are building new star but to me this looks exactly like any of the paperback pulp fiction crimi stories sold on the newspapers stand.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16414367686480685593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3168436574?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nigel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nigel" href="/user/show/61463964-nigel">Nigel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099546764" href="/book/show/6756990-the-devil-s-star">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like Ian Rankin's Rebus books</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61463964-nigel?shelf=police-procedural">police-procedural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61463964-nigel?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61463964-nigel?shelf=translated-to-english">translated-to-english</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3168436574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10919978234183118832">This series continues to get better. A mix of genuine thriller and police procedural, this one interweaves the main plot of a serial killer in Oslo during a brutally hot Norwegian summer, and Harry Hole's spiralling personal life, as well as his vendetta against his nemesis and rising star of the police department. Clever, well-paced and with some genuine thrills. Highly recommended.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1714278323" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1714278323" />
    <a title="Ivana Books Are Magic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56173179-ivana-books-are-magic"><img alt="Ivana Books Are Magic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578249636p2/56173179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1714278323?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivana Books Are Magic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivana Books Are Magic" href="/user/show/56173179-ivana-books-are-magic">Ivana Books Are Magic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9789531957977" href="/book/show/11599039-avolja-zvijezda">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1714278323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2968612843916652003">This was my first novel by Jo Nesbo but I think is safe to say that it won't be my last. I must say, I took to Nesbo's style of writing like duck to water. I felt an instant connection with the story. Very quickly into the novel, I felt transported into this world of his creation and more than willing to play the guessing game. For what makes crime novels so delicious if not the way they make our mind try to put the pieces together?<br/><br/><br/>I really liked the protagonist of this novel, the drinking detec</span>
  <span id="freeText2968612843916652003" style="display:none">This was my first novel by Jo Nesbo but I think is safe to say that it won't be my last. I must say, I took to Nesbo's style of writing like duck to water. I felt an instant connection with the story. Very quickly into the novel, I felt transported into this world of his creation and more than willing to play the guessing game. For what makes crime novels so delicious if not the way they make our mind try to put the pieces together?<br /><br /><br />I really liked the protagonist of this novel, the drinking detective, and found him to be a well-rounded character, despite of all his flaws or perhaps, precisely because of them. I'm sure I wouldn't like to know or work with this high functioning alcoholic (that often turns into a non-functioning drunk in this story) but I loved reading about him. There were a few instances when he really annoyed me, for example, when he failed to take the security of innocent people in question, but more often than not, he was a character I could relate to. Moreover, he was a character I cared about and I did feel an interest in what his fate might be. I was cheering for him to sort out his life and find the murderer.<br /><br /><br />The plot was very interesting with a lot of unexpected twists and turns. Some of them were not 100 percent bullet proof but the story works well enough and there was never a dull moment, so I’m not complaining too much. While I did start to feel impatient towards the end of the novel, there was never that feeling of frustration that sometimes comes over me when novel goes astray. This crime story didn’t get from the hand of the writer. However, I must say there were moments when it seemed it might.<br /><br /><br />It is not a great piece of writing. It's a bit too raw, too eventful with just a tad too much sparkling of clichés. The author takes us along some blind allies and while I get that he does it so that we can enjoy the ride more and feel a genuine surprise or perhaps shock as the events unfold, I still think the writer has kept us too much in the dark. Sometimes a subtle clue could have mean a lot. I felt like I was manipulated into believing in one thing, only to discover that I was utterly wrong. Not that I mind a bit of manipulation, but I prefer it to be done in a subtle and less raw way. At times it even felt like cheating and taking the easy road.<br /><br />The same could be said for some other aspects of this novel. Some characters were obviously crafted with more care than others. Just like it was the case with multiple story lines and possible answers to the riddle, for some of the characters I cared more, for some less. This novel has its ups and downs. It all ties pretty well in the end, but I can’t say that it is a great crime novel because I had read better. I did enjoy reading it and if anyone is wondering I have read it fairy recently on my vacation that is only a few days ago. For me personally, it was the perfect beach read. Light, entertaining and decent writing. I’m looking forward to reading more novels by this author.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2968612843916652003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CtZj8iwUEL8eyad0EeABRsSoBLdYtFx51mrTE0s5QiObWUrKNjmagDduDvAFuueJSvAtMrHIUsq5zyUNLiYCGQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lQIuu0iN2fERPU2ezfWz6Rtoo+ydQsNxB9lKDoqXrAoEjQeDUqBTzjia5BrZr1UmlTCKaXQ+zcJofLwQ74jsMA==')})

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17250056956247363896">Jo Nesbø is a bestselling Norwegian author and musician. He was born in Oslo and grew up in Molde. Nesbø graduated from the Norwegian School of Economics with a degree in economics. Nesbø is primarily famous for his crime novels about Detective Harry Hole, but he is also the main vocals and songwriter for the Norwegian rock band Di Derre. In 2007 Nesbø also released his first children's book, Dokt</span>
  <span id="freeText17250056956247363896" style="display:none">Jo Nesbø is a bestselling Norwegian author and musician. He was born in Oslo and grew up in Molde. Nesbø graduated from the Norwegian School of Economics with a degree in economics. Nesbø is primarily famous for his crime novels about Detective Harry Hole, but he is also the main vocals and songwriter for the Norwegian rock band Di Derre. In 2007 Nesbø also released his first children's book, Doktor Proktors Prompepulver.<br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/51155-harry-hole" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Hole</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/66741-doktor-proktor" rel="nofollow noopener">Doktor Proktor</a><br /><br />For exclusive content about Jo Nesbø and his books, register for the official fan newsletter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://jonesbo.com/newsletter/">https://jonesbo.com/newsletter/</a></span>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;It was as if the demise of the owner had lent the flat a physical void it hadn't had before. At the same time he had the feeling that he wasn't alone. Harry believed in the existence of the soul. Not that he was particularly religious as such, but it was one thing which always struck him when he saw a dead body: the body was bereft of something...the creature had gone, the light had gone,there was not the illusory afterglow that long-since burned-out stars have. The body was missing its soul and it was the absence of the soul that made Harry believe.&rdquo;</span>
